Musk\nRelatives\nMusk family\nEducation\nUniversity of Pennsylvania\n(\nBA\n,\nBS\n)\nOccupation\nCEO and product architect of\nTesla\nFounder, CEO, and chief engineer of\nSpaceX\nOwner, CTO and Musk\'s Crash Course\nRelated\nTesla Roadster in space\nTesla Takedown\nTSLAQ\nTwitter Files\n2022 Twitter suspensions\nList of Tesla Autopilot crashes\nv\nt\ne\nElon Reeve Musk\n(\n/\nˈ\niː\nl\nɒ\nn\n/\nEE\n-lon\n; born June 28, 1971) is a businessman known for\nhis key roles\nin\nTesla\n,\nSpaceX\n, and\nTwitter\n(which he\nrebranded as X\n). Since 2025, he has been a\nsenior advisor\nto United States president\nDonald Trump\nand the\nde facto\nhead of the\nDepartment of Government Efficiency\n(DOGE). Musk is the\nwealthiest person in the world\n; as of March\xa02025,\n[update]\nForbes\nestimates\nhis net worth\nto be US$330\xa0billion.\nBorn to\na wealthy family\nin\nPretoria\n, South Africa, in 1989 Musk emigrated to Canada, whose citizenship he had inherited through his mother. He graduated from the\nUniversity of Pennsylvania\nin the U.S. before moving to\nCalifornia\nto pursue business ventures. In 1995, Musk co-founded the software company\nZip2\n. Following its sale in 1999, he co-founded\nX.com\n, an online payment company that later merged to form\nPayPal\n, which was acquired by\neBay\nin 2002 for $1.5 billion. That year, Musk also became a U.S. citizen.\nIn 2002, Musk founded SpaceX and became its CEO and chief engineer. The company has since led innovations in\nreusable rockets\nand\ncommercial spaceflight\n. In 2004, Musk joined Tesla, Inc., as an early investor, and became its CEO and product architect in 2008; it has become a market leader in\nelectric vehicles\n. In 2015, he co-founded\nOpenAI\nto advance\nartificial intelligence\nresearch, but left its board in 2018. In 2016, Musk co-founded\nNeuralink\n, a company focused on\nbrain–computer interfaces\n, and in 2017 launched\nthe Boring Company\n, which aims to develop tunnel transportation. Musk was named\nTime\nmagazine\'s Person of the Year\nin 2021. In 2022, he acquired Twitter, implementing significant changes and rebranding it as X in 2023. In January 2025, he was appointed head of Trump\'s newly created DOGE.\nMusk\'s political activities\nand\nviews\nhave made him\na polarizing figure\n. He has been criticized for making unscientific and misleading statements, including\nCOVID-19 misinformation\nand\npromoting conspiracy theories\n. His acquisition of Twitter (now X) was controversial due to a subsequent\nincrease in hate speech\nand the\nspread of misinformation\non the service. He has engaged in political activities in several countries, including as a vocal and financial supporter of Trump. Musk was the largest donor in the\n2024 U.S. presidential election\nand is a supporter of global\nfar-right\nfigures, causes, and political parties.\nEarly life\nSee also:\nMusk family\nElon Reeve Musk was born on June 28, 1971, in\nPretoria\n, South Africa\'s administrative capital.\n[\n2\n]\n[\n3\n]\nHe is of British and\nPennsylvania Dutch\nancestry.\n[\n4\n]\n[\n5\n]\nHis mother,\nMaye\n(\nnée\nHaldeman\n), is a model and dietitian born in\nSaskatchewan\n, Canada, and raised in South Africa.\n[\n6\n]\n[\n7\n]\n[\n8\n]\n[\na\n]\nHis father,\nErrol Musk\n, is a South African\nelectromechanical engineer\n, pilot, sailor, consultant,\nemerald\ndealer, and property developer, who partly owned a rental lodge at\nTimbavati Private Nature Reserve\n.\n[\n14\n]\n[\n15\n]\n[\n16\n]\n[\n17\n]\nElon has a younger brother,\nKimbal\n, a younger sister,\nTosca\n, and four paternal half-siblings.\n[\n18\n]\n[\n19\n]\n[\n8\n]\n[\n20\n]\nMusk was raised in the\nAnglican Church\n, in which he was\nbaptized\n.\n[\n21\n]\n[\n22\n]\nThe Musk family was wealthy during Elon\'s youth.\n[\n17\n]\nDespite both Elon and Errol previously stating that Errol was a part owner of a Zambian emerald mine,\n[\n17\n]\nin 2023, Errol recounted that the deal he made was to receive "a portion of the emeralds produced at three small mines".\n[\n23\n]\n[\n24\n]\nErrol was elected to the Pretoria City Council as a representative of the anti-apartheid\nProgressive Party\nand has said that his children shared their father\'s dislike of\napartheid\n.\n[\n2\n]\nAfter his parents divorced in 1980, Elon chose to live primarily with his father.\n[\n4\n]\n[\n14\n]\nElon later regretted his decision and became estranged from his father.\n[\n25\n]\nElon has recounted trips to a wilderness school that he described as a "paramilitary\nLord of the Flies\n" where "bullying was a virtue" and children were encouraged to fight over rations.\n[\n26\n]\nIn one incident, after an altercation with a fellow pupil, Elon was thrown down concrete steps and beaten severely, leading to him being hospitalized for his injuries.\n[\n27\n]\nElon described his father berating him after he was discharged from the hospital.\n[\n27\n]\nErrol denied berating Elon and claimed, "The boy had just lost his father to suicide and Elon had called him stupid. Elon had a tendency to call people stupid. How could I possibly blame that child?"\n[\n28\n]\nElon was an enthusiastic reader of books, and had attributed his success in part to having read\nThe Lord of the Rings\n, the\nFoundation\nseries\n, and\nThe Hitchhiker\'s Guide to the Galaxy\n.\n[\n16\n]\n[\n29\n]\nAt age ten, he developed an interest in computing and video games, teaching himself how to program from the\nVIC-20\nuser manual.\n[\n30\n]\nAt age twelve, Elon sold his\nBASIC\n-based game\nBlastar\nto\nPC and Office Technology\nmagazine for approximately $500.\n[\n31\n]\n[\n32\n]\nEducation\nMusk graduated from\nPretoria Boys High School\nin South Africa.\nMusk attended\nWaterkloof House Preparatory School\n,\nBryanston High School\n, and then\nPretoria Boys High School\n, where he graduated.\n[\n33\n]\nMusk was a good but unexceptional student, earning a 61 in\nAfrikaans\nand a B on his senior math certification.\n[\n34\n]\nMusk applied for a Canadian passport\nthrough\nhis Canadian-born mother to avoid South Africa\'s\nmandatory military service\n,\n[\n35\n]\n[\n36\n]\nwhich would have forced him to participate in the apartheid regime,\n[\n2\n]\nas well as to ease his path to immigration to the United States.\n[\n37\n]\nWhile waiting for his application to be processed, he attended the\nUniversity of Pretoria\nfor five months.\n[\n38\n]\nMusk arrived in Canada in June 1989, connected with a second cousin in Saskatchewan,\n[\n39\n]\n[\n40\n]\nand worked odd jobs including at a farm and a lumber mill.\n[\n41\n]\nIn 1990, he entered\nQueen\'s University\nin\nKingston, Ontario\n.\n[\n42\n]\n[\n43\n]\nTwo years later, he transferred to the\nUniversity of Pennsylvania\n, where he studied until 1995.\n[\n44\n]\nAlthough Musk has said that he earned his degrees in 1995, the University of Pennsylvania did not award them until 1997 – a\nBachelor of Arts\nin physics and a\nBachelor of Science\nin economics from the university\'s\nWharton School\n.\n[\n45\n]\n[\n46\n]\n[\n47\n]\n[\n48\n]\n[\n49\n]\nHe reportedly hosted large, ticketed house parties to help pay for tuition, and wrote a business plan for an electronic book-scanning service similar to\nGoogle Books\n.\n[\n50\n]\nIn 1994, Musk held two internships in\nSilicon Valley\n: one at energy storage startup Pinnacle Research Institute, which investigated electrolytic\nsupercapacitors\nfor energy storage, and another at\nPalo Alto\n–based startup\nRocket Science Games\n.\n[\n51\n]\n[\n52\n]\nIn 1995, he was accepted to a graduate program in\nmaterials science\nat\nStanford University\n, but did not enroll.\n[\n47\n]\n[\n45\n]\n[\n53\n]\nMusk decided to join the\nInternet boom\n, applying for a job at\nNetscape\n, to which he reportedly never received a response.\n[\n54\n]\n[\n35\n]\nThe Washington Post\nreported that Musk lacked legal authorization to remain and work in the United States after failing to enroll at Stanford.\n[\n53\n]\nIn response, Musk said he was allowed to work at that time and that his student visa transitioned to an\nH1-B\n. According to numerous former business associates and shareholders, Musk said he was on a student visa at the time.\n[\n55\n]\nBusiness career\nMain article:\nBusiness career of Elon Musk\nZip2\nMain article:\nZip2\nExternal videos\nMusk speaks of his early business experience during a 2014 commencement speech at University of Southern California\non YouTube\nIn 1995, Musk, his brother Kimbal, and Greg Kouri founded web software company\nZip2\nwith funds borrowed from Musk\'s father.\n[\n56\n]\n[\n25\n]\nThey housed the venture at a small rented office in Palo Alto.\n[\n57\n]\nThe company developed and marketed an Internet city guide for the newspaper publishing industry, with maps, directions, and yellow pages.\n[\n58\n]\nAccording to Musk, "The website was up during the day and I was coding it at night, seven days a week, all the time."\n[\n57\n]\nThe Musk brothers obtained contracts with\nThe New York Times\nand the\nChicago Tribune\n,\n[\n59\n]\nand persuaded the board of directors to abandon plans for a merger with\nCitySearch\n.\n[\n60\n]\nMusk\'s attempts to become CEO were thwarted by the board.\n[\n61\n]\nCompaq\nacquired Zip2 for $307 million in cash in February 1999,\n[\n62\n]\n[\n63\n]\nand Musk received $22 million for his 7-percent share.\n[\n64\n]\nX.com and PayPal\nMain articles:\nX.com (bank)\n,\nPayPal\n, and\nPayPal Mafia\nIn 1999, Musk co-founded\nX.com\n, an online financial services and e-mail payment company.\n[\n65\n]\nThe startup was one of the first\nfederally insured\nonline banks, and, in its initial months of operation, over 200,000 customers joined the service.\n[\n66\n]\nThe company\'s investors regarded Musk as inexperienced and replaced him with\nIntuit\nCEO Bill Harris by the end of the year.\n[\n67\n]\nThe following year, X.com merged with online bank\nConfinity\nto avoid competition.\n[\n57\n]\n[\n67\n]\n[\n68\n]\nFounded by\nMax Levchin\nand\nPeter Thiel\n,\n[\n69\n]\nConfinity had its own money-transfer service,\nPayPal\n, which was more popular than X.com\'s service.\n[\n70\n]\nWithin the merged company, Musk returned as CEO. Musk\'s preference for\nMicrosoft\nsoftware over\nUnix\ncreated a rift in the company and caused Thiel to resign.\n[\n71\n]\nDue to resulting technological issues and lack of a cohesive business model, the board ousted Musk and replaced him with Thiel in 2000.\n[\n72\n]\n[\nb\n]\nUnder Thiel, the company focused on the PayPal service and was renamed PayPal in 2001.\n[\n74\n]\n[\n75\n]\nIn 2002, PayPal was acquired by\neBay\nfor $1.5\xa0billion in stock, of which Musk—the largest shareholder with 11.72% of shares—received $175.8\xa0million.\n[\n76\n]\n[\n77\n]\nIn 2017, Musk purchased the domain X.com from PayPal for an undisclosed amount, stating that it had sentimental value.\n[\n78\n]\n[\n79\n]\nSpaceX\nMain article:\nSpaceX\nMusk explains\nStarship\ncapabilities to leaders of\nNorth American Aerospace Defense Command\n, U.S. Northern Command, and\nAir Force Space Command\nin 2019\nIn 2001, Musk became involved with the nonprofit\nMars Society\nand discussed funding plans to place a\ngrowth-chamber for plants\non\nMars\n.\n[\n80\n]\nSeeking a way to launch the greenhouse payloads into space, Musk made two unsuccessful trips to Moscow to purchase\nintercontinental ballistic missiles\n(ICBMs) from Russian companies\nNPO Lavochkin\nand\nKosmotras\n. Musk instead decided to start a company to build affordable rockets.\n[\n81\n]\nWith $100\xa0million of his early fortune,\n[\n82\n]\nMusk founded SpaceX in May 2002 and became the company\'s CEO and Chief Engineer.\n[\n83\n]\n[\n84\n]\nSpaceX attempted its first launch of the\nFalcon 1\nrocket in 2006.\n[\n85\n]\nAlthough the rocket failed to reach\nEarth orbit\n, it was awarded a\nCommercial Orbital Transportation Services\nprogram contract from\nNASA\n, then led by\nMike Griffin\n.\n[\n86\n]\n[\n87\n]\nAfter two more failed attempts that nearly caused Musk to go bankrupt,\n[\n85\n]\nSpaceX succeeded in launching the Falcon 1 into orbit in 2008.\n[\n88\n]\nLater that year, SpaceX received a $1.6\xa0billion NASA contract for\nFalcon 9\n-launched\nDragon spacecraft\nflights to the\nInternational Space Station\n(ISS), replacing the\nSpace Shuttle\nafter its 2011\nretirement\n.\n[\n89\n]\nIn 2012, the Dragon vehicle docked\nwith the ISS\n, a first for a commercial spacecraft.\n[\n90\n]\nWorking towards its goal of\nreusable rockets\n, in 2015 SpaceX successfully landed the\nfirst stage\nof a Falcon 9 on a land platform.\n[\n91\n]\nLater landings were achieved on\nautonomous spaceport drone ships\n, an ocean-based recovery platform.\n[\n92\n]\nIn 2018, SpaceX launched the\nFalcon Heavy\n; the\ninaugural mission\ncarried Musk\'s personal\nTesla Roadster\nas a\ndummy payload\n.\n[\n93\n]\n[\n94\n]\nSince 2019,\n[\n95\n]\nSpaceX has been developing\nStarship\n, a reusable,\nsuper heavy-lift launch vehicle\nintended to replace the Falcon 9 and Falcon Heavy.\n[\n96\n]\nIn 2020, SpaceX launched its first crewed flight, the\nDemo-2\n, becoming the first private company to place astronauts into orbit and dock a crewed spacecraft with the ISS.\n[\n97\n]\nIn 2024, NASA awarded SpaceX an $843 million contract to\ndeorbit\nthe ISS at the end of its lifespan.\n[\n98\n]\nStarlink\nMain article:\nStarlink\nSee also:\nStarlink in the Russo-Ukrainian War\n50 Starlink satellites shortly before deployment to low Earth orbit, 2019\nIn 2015, SpaceX began development of the\nStarlink\nconstellation of\nlow Earth orbit\nsatellites to provide\nsatellite Internet access\n.\n[\n99\n]\nAfter the launch of prototype satellites in 2018, the first large constellation was deployed in May 2019.\n[\n100\n]\nThe total cost of the decade-long project to design, build, and deploy the constellation was estimated by SpaceX in 2020 to be $10\xa0billion.\n[\n101\n]\n[\nc\n]\nDuring the\nRussian invasion of Ukraine\n, Musk provided free\nStarlink service to Ukraine\n, permitting Internet access and communication at a yearly cost to SpaceX of $400\xa0million.\n[\n104\n]\n[\n105\n]\n[\n106\n]\n[\n107\n]\n[\n108\n]\nHowever, Musk refused to block\nRussian state media\non Starlink.\n[\n109\n]\n[\n110\n]\nIn 2023, Musk denied Ukraine\'s request to activate Starlink over\nCrimea\nto aid an attack against the Russian navy, citing fears of a nuclear response.\n[\n111\n]\n[\n112\n]\n[\n113\n]\nTesla\nMain article:\nTesla, Inc.\nMusk next to a\nTesla Model S\n, 2011\nTesla, Inc.\n, originally Tesla Motors, was incorporated in July 2003 by\nMartin Eberhard\nand\nMarc Tarpenning\n. Both men played active roles in the company\'s early development prior to Musk\'s involvement.\n[\n114\n]\nMusk led the\nSeries A round\nof investment in February 2004; he invested $6.35\xa0million, became the majority shareholder, and joined Tesla\'s board of directors as chairman.\n[\n115\n]\n[\n116\n]\nMusk took an active role within the company and oversaw\nRoadster\nproduct design, but was not deeply involved in day-to-day business operations.\n[\n117\n]\nFollowing a series of escalating conflicts in 2007, and the\nfinancial crisis of 2007–2008\n, Eberhard was ousted from the firm.\n[\n118\n]\n[\npage\xa0needed\n]\n[\n119\n]\nMusk assumed leadership of the company as CEO and product architect in 2008.\n[\n120\n]\nA 2009 lawsuit settlement with Eberhard designated Musk as a Tesla co-founder, along with Tarpenning and two others.\n[\n121\n]\n[\n122\n]\nTesla began delivery of the Roadster, an electric sports car, in 2008. With sales of about 2,500 vehicles, it was the first\nmass production\nall-electric car to use\nlithium-ion battery\ncells.\n[\n123\n]\nUnder Musk, Tesla has since launched several well-selling electric vehicles, including the four-door sedan\nModel S\n(2012), the\ncrossover\nModel\xa0X\n(2015), the mass-market sedan\nModel\xa03\n(2017), the crossover\nModel\xa0Y\n(2020), and the pickup truck\nCybertruck\n(2023).\n[\n124\n]\n[\n125\n]\n[\n126\n]\n[\n127\n]\n[\n128\n]\nIn May 2020 Musk resigned from chairman of the board as part of the settlement of a\nlawsuit from the SEC\nover him tweeting that funding had been "secured" for potentially taking Tesla private.\n[\n129\n]\n[\n130\n]\nThe company has also constructed multiple lithium-ion battery and electric vehicle factories, called\nGigafactories\n.\n[\n131\n]\nSince its\ninitial public offering\nin 2010,\n[\n132\n]\nTesla stock has risen significantly; it became the most valuable carmaker in summer 2020,\n[\n133\n]\n[\n134\n]\nand it entered the\nS&P 500\nlater that year.\n[\n135\n]\n[\n136\n]\nIn October 2021, it reached a market capitalization of $1\xa0trillion, the sixth company in U.S. history to do so.\n[\n137\n]\nSolarCity and Tesla Energy\nMain articles:\nSolarCity\nand\nTesla Energy\nSolarCity solar-panel installation vans in 2009\nMusk provided the initial concept and financial capital for\nSolarCity\n, which his cousins\nLyndon\nand Peter Rive founded in 2006.\n[\n138\n]\nBy 2013, SolarCity was the second largest provider of solar power systems in the United States.\n[\n139\n]\nIn 2014, Musk promoted the idea of SolarCity building an advanced production facility in\nBuffalo\n, New York, triple the size of the largest solar plant in the United States.\n[\n140\n]\nConstruction of the\nfactory\nstarted in 2014 and was completed in 2017. It operated as a joint venture with\nPanasonic\nuntil early 2020.\n[\n141\n]\n[\n142\n]\nTesla acquired SolarCity for $2\xa0billion in 2016 and merged it with its battery unit to create\nTesla Energy\n. The deal\'s announcement resulted in a more than 10% drop in Tesla\'s stock price; at the time, SolarCity was facing liquidity issues.\n[\n143\n]\nMultiple shareholder groups filed a lawsuit against Musk and Tesla\'s directors, stating that the purchase of SolarCity was done solely to benefit Musk and came at the expense of Tesla and its shareholders.\n[\n144\n]\n[\n145\n]\nTesla directors settled the lawsuit in January 2020, leaving Musk the sole remaining defendant.\n[\n146\n]\n[\n147\n]\nTwo years later, the court ruled in Musk\'s favor.\n[\n148\n]\nNeuralink\nMain article:\nNeuralink\nMusk discussing a\nNeuralink\ndevice during a live demonstration in 2020\nIn 2016, Musk co-founded\nNeuralink\n, a\nneurotechnology\nstartup, with an investment of $100\xa0million.\n[\n149\n]\n[\n150\n]\nNeuralink aims to integrate the human brain with\nartificial intelligence\n(AI) by creating devices that are embedded in the brain. Such technology could enhance memory or allow the devices to communicate with software.\n[\n150\n]\n[\n151\n]\nThe company also hopes to develop devices to treat neurological conditions like\nspinal cord injuries\n.\n[\n152\n]\nIn 2022, Neuralink announced that clinical trials would begin by the end of the year.\n[\n153\n]\nIn September 2023, the\nFood and Drug Administration\napproved Neuralink to initiate six-year human trials.\n[\n154\n]\nNeuralink has conducted\nanimal testing\non\nmacaques\nat the\nUniversity of California, Davis\n. In 2021, the company released a video in which a macaque played the video game\nPong\nvia a Neuralink implant. The company\'s animal trials—which have caused the deaths of some monkeys—have led to claims of\nanimal cruelty\n. The\nPhysicians Committee for Responsible Medicine\nhas alleged that Neuralink violated the\nAnimal Welfare Act\n.\n[\n155\n]\nEmployees have complained that pressure from Musk to accelerate development has led to botched experiments and unnecessary animal deaths. In 2022, a federal probe was launched into possible animal welfare violations by Neuralink.\n[\n156\n]\nThe Boring Company\nMain article:\nThe Boring Company\nMusk during the 2018 inauguration of the\nBoring test tunnel\nin\nHawthorne, California\nIn 2017, Musk founded the Boring Company to construct tunnels, and revealed plans for specialized, underground, high-occupancy vehicles that could travel up to 150 miles per hour (240\xa0km/h) and thus circumvent above-ground traffic in major cities.\n[\n157\n]\n[\n158\n]\nEarly in 2017, the company began discussions with regulatory bodies and initiated construction of a 30-foot (9.1\xa0m) wide, 50-foot (15\xa0m) long, and 15-foot (4.6\xa0m) deep "test trench" on the premises of SpaceX\'s offices, as that required no permits.\n[\n159\n]\nThe\nLos Angeles tunnel\n, less than two miles (3.2\xa0km) in length, debuted to journalists in 2018. It used Tesla Model\xa0Xs and was reported to be a rough ride while traveling at suboptimal speeds.\n[\n160\n]\nTwo tunnel projects announced in 2018, in Chicago and West Los Angeles, have been canceled.\n[\n161\n]\n[\n162\n]\nHowever, a tunnel beneath the\nLas Vegas Convention Center\nwas completed in early 2021.\n[\n163\n]\nLocal officials have approved further expansions of the tunnel system.\n[\n164\n]\nX Corp.\nMain articles:\nAcquisition of Twitter by Elon Musk\nand\nTwitter under Elon Musk\nAvatar of Elon Musk\nElon Musk\n@elonmusk\nI made an offer\nhttps://sec.gov/Archives/edgar...\nApril 14, 2022\n[\n165\n]\nIn early 2017, Musk expressed interest in buying\nTwitter\nand had questioned the platform\'s commitment to\nfreedom of speech\n.\n[\n166\n]\n[\n167\n]\n[\n168\n]\nBy 2022, Musk had reached 9.2% stake in the company,\n[\n169\n]\nmaking him the largest shareholder.\n[\n170\n]\n[\nd\n]\nMusk later agreed to a deal that would appoint him to Twitter\'s board of directors and prohibit him from acquiring more than 14.9% of the company.\n[\n172\n]\n[\n173\n]\nDays later, Musk made a $43 billion offer to buy Twitter.\n[\n170\n]\n[\n174\n]\nBy the end of April Musk had successfully concluded his bid for approximately $44\xa0billion.\n[\n175\n]\nThis included approximately $12.5 billion in loans and $21 billion in\nequity financing\n.\n[\n176\n]\n[\n177\n]\nHaving back tracked on his initial decision,\n[\n178\n]\nMusk bought the company on October 27, 2022.\n[\n179\n]\nImmediately\nafter the acquisition\n, Musk fired several top Twitter executives including CEO\nParag Agrawal\n;\n[\n179\n]\n[\n180\n]\nMusk became the CEO instead.\n[\n181\n]\nUnder Elon Musk\n, Twitter instituted monthly subscription for a "\nblue check\n",\n[\n182\n]\n[\n183\n]\n[\n184\n]\nand laid off a significant portion of the company\'s staff.\n[\n185\n]\n[\n186\n]\nMusk lessened content moderation and hate speech also increased on the platform after his takeover.\n[\n187\n]\n[\n188\n]\n[\n189\n]\n[\n190\n]\nIn late 2022, Musk released\ninternal documents\nrelating to Twitter\'s moderation of\nHunter Biden\'s laptop controversy\nin the lead-up to the\n2020 presidential election\n.\n[\n191\n]\nMusk also promised to step down as CEO after a Twitter poll,\n[\n192\n]\n[\n193\n]\nand five months later, Musk stepped down from\nchief executive officer\n(CEO)  and transitioned his role to\nexecutive chairman\nand\nchief technology officer\n(CTO).\n[\n194\n]\nDespite Musk stepping down as\nCEO\n, X continues to struggle with challenges such as viral\nmisinformation\n,\n[\n195\n]\nhate speech\n, and\nantisemitism\ncontroversies.\n[\n196\n]\n[\n197\n]\nMusk has been accused of\ntrying to silence some of his critics\n[\n198\n]\nby removing their accounts\'\nblue checkmarks\n, which hinders visibility and is considered a form of\nshadow banning\n,\n[\n199\n]\n[\n200\n]\nor suspending their accounts without justification.\n[\n201\n]\nOther activities\nHyperloop\nMain articles:\nHyperloop\nand\nHyperloop pod competition\nA tube part of the 2017 Hyperloop pod competition, sponsored by SpaceX\nIn August 2013, Musk announced plans for a version of a\nvactrain\n, and assigned engineers from SpaceX and Tesla to design a transport system between\nGreater Los Angeles\nand the\nSan Francisco Bay Area\n, at an estimated cost of $6 billion.\n[\n202\n]\n[\n203\n]\nLater that year, Musk unveiled the concept, dubbed the\nHyperloop\n,\n[\n204\n]\nintended to make travel cheaper than any other\nmode of transport\nfor such long distances.\n[\n205\n]\nOpenAI and xAI\nFurther information:\nOpenAI\nand\nxAI (company)\nIn December 2015, Musk co-founded\nOpenAI\n, a\nnot-for-profit\nartificial intelligence\n(AI) research company aiming to develop\nartificial general intelligence\n, intended to be safe and beneficial to humanity.\n[\n206\n]\nMusk pledged $1 billion of funding to the company,\n[\n207\n]\nbut only donated $50 million.\n[\n208\n]\nIn 2018, Musk left the OpenAI board.\n[\n209\n]\nSince 2018, OpenAI has made significant advances in machine learning.\n[\n210\n]\nIn July 2023, Musk launched the artificial intelligence company\nxAI\n, which aims to develop a\ngenerative AI\nprogram that competes with existing offerings like OpenAI\'s\nChatGPT\n. Musk obtained funding from investors in SpaceX and Tesla,\n[\n211\n]\nand xAI hired engineers from Google and OpenAI.\n[\n212\n]\nPrivate jet\nMain articles:\nElonJet\nand\n2022 Twitter suspensions\nAvatar of Elon Musk\nElon Musk\n@elonmusk\nSame doxxing rules apply to "journalists" as to everyone else\nDecember 16, 2022\n[\n213\n]\nMusk uses a private jet owned by Falcon Landing LLC, a SpaceX-linked company, and acquired a second jet in August 2020.\n[\n214\n]\n[\n215\n]\nHis heavy use of the jets and the consequent\nfossil fuel\nusage have received criticism.\n[\n214\n]\n[\n216\n]\nMusk\'s flight usage is tracked on social media through\nElonJet\n.\n[\n217\n]\n[\n218\n]\n[\n219\n]\nIn December 2022, Musk banned the ElonJet account on Twitter, as well as temporary bans on the accounts of journalists that posted stories regarding the incident, including\nDonie O\'Sullivan\n,\nKeith Olbermann\n, and journalists from\nThe New York Times\n,\nThe Washington Post\n, CNN, and\nThe Intercept\n.\n[\n220\n]\nPolitics\nMain article:\nPolitical activities of Elon Musk\nMusk with then-president-elect\nDonald Trump\nin November 2024\nMusk is an outlier among executives who typically avoid partisan political advocacy.\n[\n221\n]\n[\n222\n]\n[\n223\n]\nMusk was a registered\nindependent voter\nwhen he lived in California.\n[\n224\n]\nHistorically, he has donated to both\nDemocrats\nand\nRepublicans\n,\n[\n225\n]\nmany of whom serve in states in which he has a vested interest.\n[\n226\n]\nBeginning in 2022, his political contributions have mostly supported Republicans, with his first vote for a Republican going to Representative\nMayra Flores\nin the\n2022 Texas\'s 34th congressional district special election\n.\n[\n227\n]\n[\n228\n]\nIn 2024, he started supporting international\nfar-right\npolitical parties, activists, and causes,\n[\n229\n]\nand has shared far-right misinformation\n[\n230\n]\n[\n231\n]\n[\n232\n]\nand numerous\nconspiracy theories\n.\n[\n233\n]\n[\n234\n]\nAs of 2024\n[update]\nhis views\nwere generally described as right-wing.\n[\n235\n]\nMusk supported\nBarack Obama\nin\n2008\nand\n2012\n,\n[\n236\n]\nHillary Clinton\nin\n2016\n,\nJoe Biden\nin\n2020\n,\n[\n237\n]\nand\nDonald Trump\nin\n2024\n.\n[\n238\n]\nIn the\n2020 Democratic Party presidential primaries\n, Musk endorsed candidate\nAndrew Yang\nand expressed support for Yang\'s proposed\nuniversal basic income\n,\n[\n239\n]\nand endorsed\nKanye West\n\'s\n2020 presidential campaign\n.\n[\n240\n]\nIn 2021, Musk publicly expressed opposition to the\nBuild Back Better Act\n, a $3.5 trillion legislative package endorsed by Joe Biden that ultimately failed to pass due to unanimous opposition from congressional Republicans and several Democrats.\n[\n241\n]\nIn 2022, Musk said he would start supporting\nRepublican Party\ncandidates,\n[\n242\n]\nand gave over $50\xa0million to\nCitizens for Sanity\n, a conservative\npolitical action committee\n.\n[\n243\n]\nIn 2023, he supported Republican\nRon DeSantis\nfor the\n2024 U.S. presidential election\n, giving $10\xa0million to his campaign,\n[\n243\n]\nand hosted DeSantis\'s campaign announcement on a\nTwitter Spaces\nevent.\n[\n244\n]\n[\n245\n]\n[\n246\n]\nFrom June 2023 to January 2024, Musk hosted a bipartisan set of X Spaces with Republican and Democratic candidates, including\nRobert F. Kennedy Jr.\n,\n[\n247\n]\nVivek Ramaswamy\n,\n[\n248\n]\nand\nDean Phillips\n.\n[\n249\n]\nMusk at a 2024 gathering with Trump and other political leaders\nBy early 2024, Musk had become a vocal and financial supporter of Donald Trump.\n[\n250\n]\nIn July 2024, after the\nattempted assassination of Donald Trump\n, Musk\nendorsed him for president\n.\n[\n251\n]\n[\n252\n]\nDuring the\npresidential campaign\n, Musk joined Trump on stage at a campaign rally,\n[\n253\n]\nand during the campaign promoted conspiracy theories and falsehoods about Democrats,\nelection fraud\n[\n254\n]\nand immigration, in support of Trump.\n[\n255\n]\n[\n256\n]\nMusk was the largest individual donor of the 2024 election.\n[\n257\n]\nMusk\'s international political actions and comments have come under increasing scrutiny and criticism, especially from the governments and leaders of France, Germany, Norway, Spain and the United Kingdom, due to his position in the\nU.S. government\n.\n[\n258\n]\n[\n259\n]\n[\n260\n]\nTrump\'s inauguration\nMain article:\nElon Musk salute controversy\nMusk giving a gesture at the\nsecond inauguration of Donald Trump\nbefore saying "My heart goes out to you. It is thanks to you that the future of civilization is assured."\n[\n261\n]\n[\n262\n]\nIn his speech during the\nsecond inauguration of Donald Trump\n, Musk thumped his right hand over his heart, fingers spread wide, and then extended his right arm out, emphatically, at an upward angle, palm down and fingers together. He then repeated the gesture to the crowd behind him. As he\nfinished the gestures\n, he said to the crowd, "My heart goes out to you. It is thanks to you that the future of civilization is assured."\n[\n261\n]\n[\n262\n]\n[\n263\n]\nThe gesture was viewed as a\nNazi\nor\nRoman salute\n[\ne\n]\nby some.\n[\n264\n]\n[\n265\n]\n[\n266\n]\nMusk derided the claims as politicized.\n[\n267\n]\n[\n268\n]\nIn a social media post, he wrote: "The \'everyone is Hitler\' attack is sooo tired",\n[\n269\n]\nbut did not explicitly deny the claims.\n[\n270\n]\nHe has since denied it.\n[\n271\n]\nIn further response to the events, Musk posted a series of puns about Nazis on Twitter.\n[\n272\n]\nVarious media outlets, including the\nAssociated Press\n, reported that regardless of what Musk meant, his gesture was widely embraced by right-wing extremists and\nneo-Nazis\n.\n[\n270\n]\n[\n273\n]\nDepartment of Government Efficiency\nMain article:\nDepartment of Government Efficiency\nElon Musk wielding a chainsaw at the\nConservative Political Action Conference\n(CPAC) conference in 2025, imitating a publicity stunt used by\nJavier Milei\nsymbolic of efficiency,\nfederal mass layoffs\nand\ntax cutting\nThe concept of DOGE emerged in a discussion between Musk and\nDonald Trump\n, and in August 2024, Trump committed to giving Musk an advisory role, with Musk accepting the offer.\n[\n274\n]\nIn November and December 2024, Musk suggested that the organization could help to cut the\nU.S. federal budget\n, consolidate the number of federal agencies,\n[\n275\n]\n[\n276\n]\nand eliminate the\nConsumer Financial Protection Bureau\n,\n[\n277\n]\n[\n278\n]\nand that its final stage would be "deleting itself".\n[\n279\n]\nIn January 2025, the organization was created by\nexecutive order\n, and Musk was designated a "\nspecial government employee\n".\n[\n280\n]\n[\n281\n]\nMusk is leading the organization and is a\nsenior advisor to the president\n,\n[\n282\n]\nalthough his\nofficial role\nis not clear.\n[\n283\n]\nIn sworn statement during a lawsuit, the director of the White House\nOffice of Administration\nstated that Musk "is not an employee of the U.S. DOGE Service or U.S. DOGE Service Temporary Organization", "is not the U.S. DOGE Service administrator", and has "no actual or formal authority to make government decisions himself".\n[\n284\n]\n[\n285\n]\nTrump said two days later that he had put Musk in charge of DOGE.\n[\n286\n]\nIn February 2025, Musk was criticized for his treatment of federal government employees,\n[\n287\n]\n[\n288\n]\n[\n289\n]\nincluding his influence over the\nmass layoffs of the federal workforce\n, and his instruction to federal government employees to report their prior week\'s work, with non-responses being deemed a resignation or warranting termination.\n[\n290\n]\n[\n291\n]\n[\n292\n]\nHe has prioritized secrecy within the organization\n[\n293\n]\nand has accused others of violating privacy laws.\n[\n280\n]\nViews\nMain article:\nViews of Elon Musk\nAvatar of Elon Musk\nElon Musk\n@elonmusk\nMy commitment to free speech extends even to not banning the account following my plane, even though that is a direct personal safety risk\nNovember 6, 2022\n[\n294\n]\nRejecting the conservative label,\n[\n295\n]\nMusk has described himself as a\npolitical moderate\n, and his views have become more\nright-wing\nover time.\n[\n296\n]\nHis views have been characterized as\nlibertarian\nand\nfar-right\n,\n[\n297\n]\n[\n298\n]\nand after his\ninvolvement in European politics\n, they have received criticism from world leaders such as\nEmmanuel Macron\nand\nOlaf Scholz\n.\n[\n299\n]\n[\n300\n]\n[\n301\n]\n[\n302\n]\nWithin the context of\nAmerican politics\n, Musk supported Democratic candidates up until 2022, at which point he voted for a Republican for the first time.\n[\n236\n]\n[\n242\n]\n[\n238\n]\nHe has stated support for\nuniversal basic income\n,\n[\n303\n]\ngun rights\n,\n[\n304\n]\nfreedom of change\n,\n[\n309\n]\nand has been a critic of\nwealth tax\n,\n[\n310\n]\nshort-selling\n,\n[\n311\n]\ngovernment subsidies\n,\n[\n312\n]\nand\nWikipedia\n.\n[\n313\n]\nAn immigrant himself, Musk has have led to accusations of\nsexism\n,\nantisemitism\n,\n[\n318\n]\n[\n319\n]\ntransphobia\n,\n[\n320\n]\ndisseminating\ndisinformation\n, and support of\nwhite pride\n.\n[\n321\n]\n[\n322\n]\nWhile migration\nand\nopen borders\n,\n[\n339\n]\n[\n340\n]\ncriticized Prime Minister\nStarmer\nfor what he described as a "two-tier" policing system,\n[\n341\n]\n[\n342\n]\n[\n343\n]\nand was subsequently support for\nReform UK\n.\n[\n345\n]\n[\n346\n]\nLegal affairs\nMain article:\nLegal affairs of Elon Musk\nFurther information:\nList of lawsuits involving Tesla, Inc.\nand\nCriticism of Tesla, Inc.\nIn 2018, Musk was\nsued\nby the\nU.S. Securities and Exchange Commission\n(SEC) for a\ntweet\nstating that funding had been secured for potentially taking Tesla private.\n[\n347\n]\n[\nf\n]\nThe securities fraud lawsuit characterized the tweet as false, misleading, and damaging to investors, and sought to bar Musk from serving as CEO of\npublicly traded companies\n.\n[\n347\n]\n[\n351\n]\n[\n352\n]\nTwo days later, Musk settled with the SEC, without admitting or denying the SEC\'s allegations. As a result, Musk and Tesla were fined $20\xa0million each, and Musk was forced to step down for three years as Tesla chairman but was able to remain as CEO.\n[\n353\n]\nShareholders filed a lawsuit over the tweet,\n[\n354\n]\nand in February 2023, a jury found Musk and Tesla not liable.\n[\n355\n]\nMusk has stated in interviews that he does not regret posting the tweet that triggered the SEC investigation.\n[\n356\n]\n[\n357\n]\nIn 2019, Musk stated in a tweet that Tesla would build half\xa0a\xa0million cars that year.\n[\n358\n]\nThe SEC reacted by asking a court to hold him\nin contempt\nfor violating the terms of the 2018 settlement agreement. A joint agreement between Musk and the SEC eventually clarified the previous agreement details,\n[\n359\n]\nincluding a list of topics about which Musk needed preclearance.\n[\n360\n]\nIn 2020, a judge blocked a lawsuit that claimed a tweet by Musk regarding Tesla stock price ("too high\nimo\n") violated the agreement.\n[\n361\n]\n[\n362\n]\nFreedom of Information Act\n(FOIA)-released records showed that the SEC concluded Musk had subsequently violated the agreement twice by tweeting regarding "\nTesla\'s solar roof\nproduction volumes and its stock price".\n[\n363\n]\nIn October 2023, the SEC sued Musk over his refusal to testify a third time in an investigation into whether he violated federal law by purchasing Twitter stock in 2022.\n[\n364\n]\n[\n365\n]\n[\n366\n]\nIn February 2024, Judge Laurel Beeler ruled that Musk must testify again.\n[\n367\n]\nIn January 2025, the SEC filed a lawsuit against Musk for securities violations related to his purchase of Twitter.\n[\n368\n]\nIn January 2024, Delaware Judge\nKathaleen McCormick\nruled in a 2018 lawsuit that Musk\'s $55\xa0billion pay package from Tesla be rescinded.\n[\n369\n]\nMcCormick called the compensation granted by the company\'s board "an unfathomable sum" that was unfair to shareholders.\n[\n370\n]\nPersonal life\nMusk became a U.S. citizen in 2002.\n[\n371\n]\nFrom the early 2000s until late 2020, Musk resided in California, where both Tesla and SpaceX were founded.\n[\n372\n]\nHe then relocated to\nCameron County, Texas\n,\n[\n373\n]\n[\n374\n]\nsaying that California had become "complacent" about its economic success.\n[\n372\n]\n[\n375\n]\n[\n376\n]\nWhile hosting\nSaturday Night Live\nin 2021, Musk stated that he has\nAsperger syndrome\n(now merged with\nautism spectrum disorder\n), although he has not been medically diagnosed.\n[\n377\n]\n[\n378\n]\nMusk suffers from back pain and has undergone several spine-related surgeries, including a\ndisc\nreplacement.\n[\n379\n]\n[\n380\n]\nIn 2000, he contracted a severe case of\nmalaria\nwhile on vacation in South Africa.\n[\n381\n]\nMusk has stated he uses doctor-prescribed\nketamine\nfor occasional depression and that he doses "a small amount once every other week or something like that";\n[\n382\n]\nsince January 2024, some media outlets have reported that he takes\nketamine\n,\nmarijuana\n,\nLSD\n,\necstasy\n,\nmushrooms\n,\ncocaine\nand other drugs. Musk at first refused to comment on his alleged drug use, before responding that he had not\ntested\npositive for drugs, and that if drugs somehow improved his productivity, "I would definitely take them!".\n[\n383\n]\nThrough his own label Emo G Records, Musk released a\nrap\ntrack, "RIP\nHarambe\n", on\nSoundCloud\nin March 2019.\n[\n384\n]\n[\n385\n]\n[\n386\n]\nThe following year, he released an\nEDM\ntrack, "Don\'t Doubt Ur Vibe", featuring his own lyrics and vocals.\n[\n387\n]\nMusk plays video games, which he stated has a "\'restoring effect\' that helps his \'mental calibration\'",\n[\n388\n]\nincluding\nQuake\n,\nDiablo IV\n,\nElden Ring\n, and\nPolytopia\n,\n[\n389\n]\n[\n390\n]\nand has admitted to "\naccount boosting\n", or cheating by hiring outside services to achieve top player rankings.\n[\n391\n]\n[\n392\n]\nRelationships and children\nFurther information:\nMusk family §\xa0Relationships and children of Elon Musk\nMusk with his son, X Æ A-Xii, in the\nOval Office\n, February 2025\nMusk has fathered fourteen children, one of whom died as an infant.\n[\n393\n]\nHe had six children with his first wife, Canadian author\nJustine Wilson\n, who he met while attending Queen\'s University in Ontario, Canada; they married in 2000.\n[\n394\n]\nIn 2002, their first child Nevada Musk died of\nsudden infant death syndrome\nat the age of 10 weeks.\n[\n395\n]\nAfter his death, the couple used\nin vitro fertilization\n(IVF) to continue their family;\n[\n396\n]\nthey had twins in 2004, followed by triplets in 2006.\n[\n396\n]\nThe couple divorced in 2008 and have\nshared custody\nof their children.\n[\n397\n]\n[\n398\n]\nThe elder twin he had with Wilson\ncame out\nas a\ntrans woman\nand, in 2022, officially\nchanged her name\nto Vivian Jenna Wilson,\n[\n399\n]\nadopting her mother\'s surname because she no longer wished to be associated with Musk.\n[\n399\n]\nMusk began dating English actress\nTalulah Riley\nin 2008.\n[\n400\n]\nThey married two years later at\nDornoch Cathedral\nin Scotland.\n[\n401\n]\n[\n402\n]\nIn 2012, the couple divorced, before remarrying the following year.\n[\n403\n]\nAfter briefly filing for divorce in 2014,\n[\n403\n]\nMusk finalized a second divorce from Riley in 2016.\n[\n404\n]\nMusk then dated\nAmber Heard\nfor several months in 2017;\n[\n405\n]\nhe had reportedly been "pursuing" her since 2012.\n[\n406\n]\nIn 2018, Musk and Canadian musician\nGrimes\nconfirmed they were dating.\n[\n407\n]\nGrimes and Musk have three children, born in 2020, 2021, and 2022.\n[\n408\n]\n[\n409\n]\n[\n410\n]\n[\n411\n]\nMusk and Grimes originally gave their eldest child the name "X\nÆ\nA-12", which would have violated California regulations as it contained characters that are not in the modern English alphabet;\n[\n412\n]\n[\n413\n]\nthe names registered on the birth certificate are "X" as a first name, "Æ A-\nXii\n" as a middle name, and "Musk" as a last name.\n[\n414\n]\n[\n415\n]\nThey received criticism for choosing a name perceived to be impractical and difficult to pronounce;\n[\n416\n]\nMusk has said the intended pronunciation is "X Ash A Twelve".\n[\n415\n]\nTheir second child was born via\nsurrogacy\n.\n[\n417\n]\nDespite the pregnancy, Musk confirmed reports that the couple were "semi-separated" in September 2021; in an interview with\nTime\nin December 2021, he said he was single.\n[\n418\n]\n[\n419\n]\nIn October 2023, Grimes sued Musk over parental rights and custody of X Æ A-Xii.\n[\n420\n]\n[\n421\n]\n[\n422\n]\nMusk also has four children with\nShivon Zilis\n, director of operations and special projects at\nNeuralink\n: twins born via\nIVF\nin 2021, a child born in 2024 via surrogacy and a child born in 2025.\n[\n423\n]\n[\n424\n]\n[\n425\n]\n[\n426\n]\n[\n427\n]\nWealth\nThese paragraphs are an excerpt from\nWealth of Elon Musk\n.\n[\nedit\n]\nElon Musk is the\nwealthiest person in the world\n, with an estimated\nnet worth\nof US$301\xa0billion as of March 10, 2025, according to the\nBloomberg Billionaires Index\n,\n[\n428\n]\nand $320\xa0billion according to\nForbes\n,\n[\n429\n]\nprimarily from his ownership stakes in\nTesla\nand\nSpaceX\n.\n[\n430\n]\nHaving been first listed on the\nForbes Billionaires List\nin 2012,\n[\n431\n]\naround 75% of Musk\'s wealth was derived from Tesla stock in November 2020.\n[\n432\n]\nDescribing himself as "\ncash poor\n",\n[\n433\n]\n[\n434\n]\na year later, he became the first person in the world to have a net worth above $300\xa0billion. By December 2024, he became the first person to reach a net worth of $400\xa0billion.\n[\n435\n]\nMusk Foundation\nMain article:\nMusk Foundation\nMusk is president of the Musk Foundation he founded in 2001,\n[\n436\n]\n[\n437\n]\nwhose stated purpose is to provide solar-power energy systems in disaster areas, with an interest in human space exploration,\npediatrics\n, renewable energy, and "safe artificial intelligence".\n[\n438\n]\nFrom 2002 to 2018, the foundation donated nearly half of its $25 million directly to Musk\'s OpenAI.\n[\n439\n]\n[\n440\n]\nThe foundation\'s assets reached $9.4 billion by the end of 2021, but it only dispensed $160 million to charities that year.\n[\n441\n]\nThe Musk Foundation has been criticized for its "self-serving"\n[\n441\n]\ndonations to efforts close to Musk\'s family and companies,\n[\n442\n]\nas well as its low payout ratio.\n[\n441\n]\n[\n443\n]\nIn 2021, after Musk challenged\nWorld Food Programme\ndirector\nDavid Beasley\nto draft a plan to use money of Musk\'s that Beasley said could contribute to ending\nworld hunger\n,\n[\n444\n]\n[\n445\n]\nMusk instead donated the $6 billion in question to his own foundation even after Beasley\'s plan showed that the money could feed 42 million people for a year.\n[\n446\n]\n[\n441\n]\n[\n447\n]\nPublic image\nMain article:\nPublic image of Elon Musk\nAlthough his ventures have been highly influential within their separate industries starting in the 2000s, Musk only became a public figure in the early 2010s. He has been described as an eccentric who makes spontaneous and impactful decisions, while also often making controversial statements, contrary to other billionaires who prefer reclusiveness to protect their businesses. Musk\'s actions and\nhis expressed views\nhave made him a polarizing figure.\n[\n448\n]\nBiographer Ashlee Vance described people\'s opinions of Musk as polarized due to his "part philosopher, part\ntroll\n" persona on Twitter.\n[\n449\n]\nDuring a\n2025 Conservative Political Action Conference\n, Musk, while wearing a gold chain, sunglasses, and holding a chainsaw, stated: "I am become\nmeme\n".\n[\n450\n]\nMusk has been described as an American\noligarch\ndue to his extensive influence over public discourse, social media, industry, politics, and government policy.\n[\n451\n]\nAfter Trump\'s re-election, Musk\'s\ninfluence and actions\nduring the transition period and the\nsecond presidency of Donald Trump\nled some to call him "President Musk", the "actual president-elect", "shadow president" or "co-president".\n[\n452\n]\n[\n453\n]\nAccolades\nMain article:\nList of awards and honors received by Elon Musk\nMusk receiving the\nOrder of Defence Merit\nfrom the\nBrazilian Armed Forces\nin 2022\n[\n454\n]\nAwards for his contributions to the development of the\nFalcon rockets\ninclude the\nAmerican Institute of Aeronautics and Astronautics\nGeorge Low Transportation Award in 2008,\n[\n455\n]\nthe\nFédération Aéronautique Internationale\nGold Space Medal in 2010,\n[\n456\n]\nand the\nRoyal Aeronautical Society\nGold Medal in 2012.\n[\n457\n]\nIn 2015, he received an honorary doctorate in engineering and technology from\nYale University\n[\n458\n]\nand an\nInstitute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers Honorary Membership\n.\n[\n459\n]\nMusk was elected a\nFellow of the Royal Society\n(FRS) in 2018.\n[\n460\n]\n[\ng\n]\nIn 2022, Musk was elected to the\nNational Academy of Engineering\n.\n[\n462\n]\nTime\nhas listed Musk as\none of the most influential people in the world\nin 2010,\n[\n463\n]\n2013,\n[\n464\n]\n2018,\n[\n465\n]\nand 2021.\n[\n466\n]\nMusk was selected as\nTime\n\'\ns "\nPerson of the Year\n" for 2021. Then\nTime\neditor-in-chief\nEdward Felsenthal\nwrote that, "Person of the Year is a marker of influence, and few individuals have had more influence than Musk on life on Earth, and potentially life off Earth too."\n[\n467\n]\n[\n468\n]\nIn popular culture\nSee also:\nElon Musk filmography\nMusk was a partial inspiration for the characterization of\nTony Stark\nin the\nMarvel\nfilm\nIron Man\n(2008).\n[\n469\n]\nMusk also had a cameo appearance in the film\'s 2010 sequel,\nIron Man 2\n.\n[\n470\n]\nOther films that he has made cameos and appearances include\nMachete Kills\n(2013),\n[\n471\n]\nWhy Him?\n(2016),\n[\n472\n]\nand\nMen in Black: International\n(2019).\n[\n473\n]\nTelevision series in which he has appeared include\nThe Simpsons\n("\nThe Musk Who Fell to Earth\n", 2015),\n[\n474\n]\nThe Big Bang Theory\n("\nThe Platonic Permutation\n", 2015),\n[\n475\n]\nSouth Park\n("\nMembers Only\n", 2016),\n[\n476\n]\n[\n477\n]\nYoung Sheldon\n("\nA Patch, a Modem, and a Zantac®\n", 2017),\n[\n478\n]\nRick and Morty\n("\nOne Crew over the Crewcoo\'s Morty\n", 2019).\n[\n479\n]\n[\n480\n]\nHe contributed interviews to the documentaries\nRacing Extinction\n(2015) and\nLo and Behold\n(2016).\n[\n481\n]\n[\n482\n]\nNotes\n^\nElon\'s maternal grandfather,\nJoshua N. Haldeman\n, who died when Elon was a toddler, was an American-born Canadian who took his family on record-breaking journeys to Africa and Australia in a single-engine\nAviaBellanca airplane\n.\n[\n9\n]\n[\n10\n]\n[\n11\n]\n[\n12\n]\nIn Canada, Haldeman was a political activist with the\nSocial Credit Party of Canada\nand the\nTechnocracy movement\n. After moving to South Africa in 1950, he wrote articles supporting\napartheid\nand far-right\nconspiracy theories\n.\n[\n13\n]\n^\nMusk remained on the board and served as an advisor.\n[\n73\n]\n[\n74\n]\n^\nSpaceX received nearly $900\xa0million in\nFederal Communications Commission\nsubsidies for Starlink.\n[\n102\n]\n[\n103\n]\n^\nHe did not file the necessary SEC paperwork within 10\xa0days of his stake passing 5%, a violation of US securities laws.\n[\n171\n]\n^\nThe "Roman salute" is a gesture which was used by\nItalian Fascists\n, then adopted by the\nNazis\n. LXXI, no. 1 (January 18, 2024), pp.\xa06, 8, 10. "There is an anti-modern impulse to Musk, a craving for lordship that can\'t be entirely satisfied within the confines of a capitalist economy. A king doesn\'t have advertisers or shareholders or customers, and Musk, if he continues on his current trajectory, may very well be abandoned by all three.\nAristotle\nsays a good ending should be surprising but inevitable. It\'s possible to imagine multiple finales for Musk that meet these criteria, but the story always begins the same way. Once upon a time in\nPretoria\n, there was a boy who wanted to be a man." also\n5\nNotes\n6\nReferences\nToggle the table of contents\nWealth of Elon Musk\n1 language\nBikol Central\nEdit links\nArticle\nTalk\nEnglish\nRead\nEdit\nView history\nTools\nTools\nmove to Tesla Autopilot crashes\nv\nt\ne\nElon Musk in 2022\nElon Musk\nis the\nwealthiest person in the world\n, with an estimated\nnet worth\nof US$301\xa0billion as of March 10, 2025, according to the\nBloomberg Billionaires Index\n,\n[\n1\n]\nand $320\xa0billion according to\nForbes\n,\n[\n2\n]\nprimarily from his ownership stakes in\nTesla\nand\nSpaceX\n.\n[\n3\n]\nHaving been first listed on the\nForbes Billionaires List\nin 2012,\n[\n4\n]\naround 75% of Musk\'s wealth was derived from Tesla stock in November 2020.\n[\n5\n]\nDescribing himself as "\ncash poor\n",\n[\n6\n]\n[\n7\n]\na year later, he became the first person in the world to have a net worth above $300\xa0billion. By December 2024, he became the first person to reach a net worth of $400\xa0billion.\n[\n8\n]\nHistory\n[\nedit\n]\nElon Musk made $175.8\xa0million when\nPayPal\nwas sold to\neBay\nin October 2002.\n[\n9\n]\nHe was first listed on the\nForbes Billionaires List\nin 2012, with a net worth of $2\xa0billion.\n[\n4\n]\nMusk paid $455\xa0million in taxes on $1.52\xa0billion of income between 2014 and 2018.\n[\n10\n]\nAccording to\nProPublica\n, Musk paid no federal income taxes in 2018.\n[\n11\n]\nHe stated his 2021 tax bill was estimated at $12\xa0billion based on his sale of $14\xa0billion worth of Tesla stock.\n[\n10\n]\nMusk has repeatedly described himself as "\ncash poor\n",\n[\n6\n]\n[\n7\n]\nand has "professed to have little interest in the material trappings of wealth".\n[\n6\n]\nIn May 2020, he pledged to sell almost all physical possessions.\n[\n7\n]\nMusk has defended his wealth by saying he is accumulating resources for\nhumanity\'s outward expansion to space\n.\n[\n12\n]\nAt the start of 2020, Elon Musk had a net worth of $27\xa0billion.\n[\n13\n]\nBy the end of the year his net worth had increased by $150\xa0billion, mostly driven by his ownership of around 20% of Tesla stock.\n[\n14\n]\nDuring this period, Musk\'s net worth was often volatile. For example, it dropped $16.3\xa0billion on September 8, the largest single-day plunge in\nBloomberg Billionaires Index\n\'\ns\nhistory at the time.\n[\n15\n]\nIn November of that year, Musk passed Facebook co-founder\nMark Zuckerberg\nto become the third-richest person in the world; a week later he passed\nMicrosoft\nco-founder\nBill Gates\nto become the second-richest.\n[\n5\n]\nIn January 2021, Musk, with a net worth of $185\xa0billion, surpassed\nAmazon\nfounder\nJeff Bezos\nto become the richest person in the world.\n[\n16\n]\nBezos reclaimed the top spot the following month.\n[\n17\n]\nOn September 27, 2021, after Tesla stock surged, Forbes announced that Musk had a net worth of over $200\xa0billion,\n[\n18\n]\nand was the richest person in the world. In November 2021, Musk became the first person to have a net worth of more than $300\xa0billion.\n[\n19\n]\nOn December 30, 2022, due to declining stock values in Tesla, Musk had lost $200\xa0billion from his net worth, the first person in history to do so,\n[\n20\n]\n[\n21\n]\nwhich was recognized by\nGuinness World Records\nin January 2023.\n[\n22\n]\nMusk\'s net worth surged after the\n2024 United States presidential election\n, and in December 2024, he became the first person to have a net worth of more than $400\xa0billion.\n[\n8\n]\nA primary customer, the\nfederal government of the United States\nhas signed contracts worth $20\xa0billion with SpaceX as of November\xa02024\n[update]\n.\n[\n23\n]\nMusk\'s association with the\nTrump administration\nreceived backlash, resulting in his net worth dropping by $126 billion between December 2024 and March 2025.\n[\n24\n]\nSources of wealth\n[\nedit\n]\nAround 75% of Musk\'s wealth was derived from Tesla stock in November 2020,\n[\n5\n]\na proportion that fell to about 37% as of December 2022,\n[\na\n]\nafter selling nearly $40\xa0billion in company shares since late 2021.\n[\n25\n]\nMusk does not receive a salary from Tesla; he agreed with the board in 2018 to a compensation plan that ties his personal earnings to Tesla\'s valuation and revenue.\n[\n14\n]\nThe deal stipulated that Musk only received the compensation if Tesla reached certain market values.\n[\n26\n]\nIt was the largest such deal ever done between a CEO and a company board.\n[\n27\n]\nIn the first award, given in May 2020, he was eligible to purchase 1.69\xa0million Tesla shares (about 1% of the company) at below-market prices, which was worth about $800\xa0million.\n[\n27\n]\n[\n26\n]\nIn January 2024, Delaware Judge\nKathaleen McCormick\nruled in a 2018 lawsuit that Musk\'s $55\xa0billion pay package from Tesla be rescinded.\n[\n28\n]\nMcCormick called the compensation granted by the company\'s board "an unfathomable sum" that was unfair to shareholders. In response to the ruling, Musk posted on X: "Never incorporate your company in the state of Delaware."\n[\n29\n]\nA re-ratification shareholders\' vote passed in mid-June 2024, although much follow-up litigation is expected, including a lawsuit filed by a Tesla investor beforehand that alleged Musk employed "coercive tactics" to move the vote in his favor.\n[\n30\n]\nManagement\n[\nedit\n]\nMusk\'s wealth is managed by his\nfamily office\ncalled Excession LLC, formed in 2016 and run by\nJared Birchall\n.\n[\n31\n]\nMusk Foundation\n[\nedit\n]\nThis section is an excerpt from\nMusk Foundation\n.\n[\nedit\n]\nThe\nMusk Foundation\nis a\nUS\n-based charitable\nfoundation\nfunded and directed primarily by\nElon Musk\n. The foundation is dedicated to promoting\nrenewable energy\n,\ncrewed space exploration\n,\npediatrics\n, science and engineering education, and the "development of safe\nartificial intelligence\nfor the benefit of humanity".\n[\n32\n]\nAt the end of 2022, the foundation had assets of US$5 billion, $4.5 billion of which were in the form of shares in the carmaker\nTesla\n.\n[\n33\n]\nGiving\n[\nedit\n]\nEducation\n[\nedit\n]\nMusk has asserted that declining\nbirth rates\npose an existential threat to humanity and in 2021 donated $10 million to the\nUniversity of Texas at Austin\nto research the potential risks.\n[\n34\n]\n[\n35\n]\nIn December 2023, tax records revealed that Musk had donated $100 million to a new foundation, "The Foundation", set up to create a primary and secondary school focused on teaching\nscience, technology, engineering, and math\n(STEM) subjects.\n[\n36\n]\n[\n37\n]\nThe foundation included plans to expand the project to the university level accredited by the\nSouthern Association of Colleges and Schools\n.\n[\n36\n]\nIn 2022, Musk allocated\nTesla, Inc.\nstock valued at $2.2\xa0billion to The Foundation.\n[\ncitation needed\n]\nTechnology\n[\nedit\n]\nIn January 2015 Musk donated $10\xa0million to the nonprofit\nFuture of Life Institute\n, an organization focused on challenges posed by advanced technologies.\n[\n38\n]\nPolitics\n[\nedit\n]\nAccording to the\nWall Street Journal\n,\nMusk donated $50 million in the fall of 2022 to\nCitizens for Sanity\n, a\npolitical action committee\n(PAC) aligned with the policies of\nDonald Trump\n.\n[\n39\n]\nMusk donated $10 million in 2023 to support the\nRon DeSantis 2024 presidential campaign\n.\n[\n40\n]\nIn 2024, Musk supported the\nDonald Trump 2024 presidential campaign\n, creating\nAmerica PAC\n[\n41\n]\nand donating $270 million to it.\n[\n42\n]\n[\n43\n]\nHe also gave $20.5 million to pro-Trump\nRBG PAC\n.\n[\n44\n]\nSee also\n[\nedit\n]\nAstra Nova School\nTexas Institute of Technology and Science\nNotes\n[\nedit\n]\n^\nAccording to\nThe Wall Street Journal\n, he was worth $140\xa0billion, with For a planned "SpaceX option package" using cold gas thrusters, see\nTesla Roadster (second generation)\n.\nElon Musk\'s Tesla Roadster\nElon Musk\'s Tesla Roadster. Earth is in the background\nNames\nSpaceX Roadster\n[\n1\n]\nStarman\n[\n1\n]\nMission type\nTest flight\nOperator\nSpaceX\nCOSPAR ID\n2018-017A\nSATCAT\nno.\n43205\nMission duration\nActive: 1 Day\nIn Orbit: 7\xa0years, 1\xa0month and 9\xa0days\nSpacecraft properties\nSpacecraft type\n2010 Tesla Roadster\n[\n2\n]\nused as a\nmass simulator\n, attached to the\nupper stage\nof a\nFalcon Heavy\nrocket\nManufacturer\nTesla\nand SpaceX\nLaunch mass\n~1,300\xa0kg (2,900\xa0lb);\n~5,900\xa0kg (13,000\xa0lb) including rocket upper stage\n[\n3\n]\nStart of mission\nLaunch date\nFebruary 6, 2018, 3:45 pm\nEST\n(20:45\nUTC\n)\nRocket\nFalcon Heavy\nFH-001\nLaunch site\nKennedy\nLC-39A\nContractor\nSpaceX\nEnd of mission\nDeactivated\nFebruary 7, 2018\nOrbital parameters\nReference\xa0system\nHeliocentric\nEccentricity\n0.25571\n[\n4\n]\nPerihelion altitude\n0.98613\nau\n(147,523,000\nkm\n)\n[\n4\n]\nAphelion altitude\n1.6637\xa0au (248,890,000\xa0km)\n[\n4\n]\nInclination\n1.077°\n[\n4\n]\nPeriod\n1.525 year\n[\n4\n]\nEpoch\n1 May 2018\nThis article is part of\na series about\nElon Musk\nPersonal\nAwards and honors\nBusiness career\nViews\nFamily\nFilmography\nInternational relations\nLegal affairs\nPublic image\nWealth\nFoundation\nPolitical activities\nCompanies\nZip2\nX.com\nPayPal\nSpaceX\nStarlink\nTesla, Musk\n(Isaacson)\nElon Musk\n(Vance)\nLudicrous\nPower Play\n"\nMembers Only\n"\n"\nThe Platonic Permutation\n"\n"\nThe Musk Who Fell to Earth\n"\n"\nOne Crew over the Crewcoo\'s Morty\n"\nElon Musk\'s Crash Course\nRelated\nTesla Roadster in space\nTesla Takedown\nTSLAQ\nTwitter Files\n2022 Twitter suspensions\nList of Tesla Autopilot crashes\nv\nt\ne\nElon Musk\'s Tesla Roadster\nis an electric sports car that served as the\ndummy payload\nfor the February 2018\nFalcon Heavy test flight\nand became an\nartificial satellite\nof the Sun. A mannequin in a\nspacesuit\n, dubbed "Starman", occupies the driver\'s seat. The car and rocket are products of\nTesla\nand\nSpaceX\n, respectively, both companies headed by\nElon Musk\n.\n[\n5\n]\nThe\n2010 Roadster\nis personally owned by and previously used by Musk for commuting to work.\n[\n2\n]\nIt is the first\nproduction car\nlaunched into space.\nThe car, mounted on the rocket\'s second stage, was launched on an\nescape trajectory\nand entered an\nelliptical\nheliocentric orbit\ncrossing the orbit of\nMars\n.\n[\n6\n]\nThe orbit reaches a maximum distance from the Sun at\naphelion\nof 1.66\nastronomical units\n(au).\n[\n4\n]\nVideo of the Roadster during the launch was transmitted back to the\nmission control center\nand live-streamed.\n[\n7\n]\nAdvertising analysts noted Musk\'s sense of\nbrand management\nand use of new media for his decision to launch a Tesla into space. Musk explained he wanted to inspire the public about the "possibility of something new happening in space" as part of his larger vision for\nspreading humanity to other planets\n.\n[\n8\n]\nBackground\n[\nedit\n]\nMusk\'s Tesla Roadster parked outside SpaceX, 2010.\nIn March 2017,\nSpaceX\n\'s founder,\nElon Musk\n, said that because the launch of the new\nFalcon Heavy\nvehicle was risky, it would carry the "silliest thing we can imagine".\n[\n9\n]\nIn June 2017, one of his Twitter followers suggested that the silly thing be a\nTesla Model S\n, to which Musk replied: "Suggestions welcome!"\n[\n10\n]\n[\n11\n]\n[\n12\n]\n[\n13\n]\nIn December 2017, Musk announced that the payload would be his personal "midnight cherry Tesla Roadster".\n[\n14\n]\n[\n15\n]\n[\n16\n]\n[\n17\n]\nOne of the test flight objectives was to demonstrate that the new rocket could carry a payload as far as the orbit of Mars.\nNASA\ndeputy administrator\nLori Garver\nstated that SpaceX had "offered free launches to NASA,\nAir Force\netc. but got no takers", and that "the Tesla gimmick was the backup".\n[\n18\n]\nThe Roadster is the first standard roadworthy vehicle sent into space,\n[\n19\n]\nfollowing several special-purpose\nlunar\nand\nMars rovers\n.\nRoadster as payload\n[\nedit\n]\nThe Roadster is permanently attached to the upper stage of the Falcon Heavy rocket.\nFalcon Heavy\nliftoff from pad\nLC-39A\n.\nThe car was permanently mounted on the rocket in an inclined position above the payload adapter. Tubular structures were added to mount front and side cameras. Photos of the car prior to payload encapsulation were released.\n[\n20\n]\nPositioned in the driver\'s seat is "Starman", a full-scale human mannequin clad in\na SpaceX pressure spacesuit\n.\n[\n21\n]\nIt was placed with the right hand on the steering wheel and the left elbow resting on the open window sill. The mannequin was named after the\nDavid Bowie\nsong "\nStarman\n",\n[\n22\n]\nand the car\'s sound system was set before launch to continuously loop the Bowie song "\nSpace Oddity\n".\n[\n23\n]\nA copy of\nDouglas Adams\n\' novel\nThe Hitchhiker\'s Guide to the Galaxy\nis in the glove box, along with references to the book in the form of a\ntowel\nand a sign on the dashboard that reads "\nDON\'T PANIC!\n".\n[\n24\n]\nA\nHot Wheels\nminiature Roadster with a miniature Starman is mounted on the dashboard. A plaque bearing the names of the employees who worked on the project is placed underneath the car, and a message on the vehicle\'s circuit board reads "Made on Earth by humans".\n[\n25\n]\nThe car carries a copy of Isaac Asimov\'s\nFoundation\ntrilogy\non a\n5D optical disc\n, a proof of concept for high-density long-lasting data storage, donated to Musk by the\nArch Mission Foundation\n.\n[\n26\n]\n[\n27\n]\nTrajectory\n[\nedit\n]\nMain article:\nFalcon Heavy test flight\nAn animation of the Roadster\'s trajectory\nSpaceX Roadster\nSun\nMercury\nVenus\nEarth\nMars\nOrbit of the Roadster, with the planets of the inner Solar System for context. Its\naphelion\nis ~250 million kilometres (1.66\nau\n).\nThe US\nOffice of Commercial Space Transportation\nissued the test flight\'s launch license on February 2, 2018.\n[\n28\n]\nThe rocket lifted off from\nLaunch Complex 39A\nat\nKennedy Space Center\n[\n28\n]\nat 15:45 EST (20:45 UTC) on February 6.\n[\n29\n]\nThe upper stage supporting the car was initially placed in an Earth\nparking orbit\n.\n[\n6\n]\nIt spent six hours coasting through the\nVan Allen radiation belts\n, thereby demonstrating a new capability requested by the\nU.S. Air Force\nfor direct insertion of heavy intelligence satellites into\ngeostationary orbit\n. Then, the upper stage performed a second boost to reach the desired\nescape trajectory\n.\n[\n30\n]\n[\n31\n]\n[\n32\n]\nThe launch was\nlive streamed\n, and video feeds from space showed the Roadster at various angles, with Earth in the background, thanks to cameras placed inside and outside the car, on booms attached to the vehicle\'s custom adaptor atop the upper stage.\n[\n33\n]\n[\n34\n]\nMusk had estimated the car\'s battery would last over 12 hours, but the live stream ran for just over four hours, thus ending before the final boost out of Earth orbit.\n[\n7\n]\n[\n35\n]\n[\n36\n]\nThe images were released by SpaceX into the\npublic domain\non their\nFlickr\naccount.\n[\n37\n]\n[\n38\n]\nFollowing the launch, the rocket stage carrying the car was given the\nSatellite Catalog Number\n43205, named "TESLA ROADSTER/FALCON 9H", along with the\nCOSPAR designation\n2018-017A.\n[\n39\n]\nThe\nJPL Horizons\nsystem publishes solutions for the trajectory as target body "-143205".\n[\n1\n]\n[\n4\n]\nThe Roadster is in a heliocentric orbit that crosses the orbit of Mars and reaches a distance of\n1.66 au\nfrom the Sun.\n[\n6\n]\nWith an inclination of roughly 1 degree to the\necliptic plane\n, compared to Mars\' 1.85° inclination, this trajectory by design cannot intercept Mars, so the car will neither\nfly by Mars\nnor enter an\norbit around Mars\n.\n[\n40\n]\nThis was the second object launched by SpaceX to leave Earth orbit, after the\nDSCOVR\nmission to the Earth–Sun\nL\n1\nLagrangian point. Nine months after launch, the Tesla had travelled beyond the orbit of Mars,\n[\n41\n]\nreaching\naphelion\nat 12:48 UTC on November 9, 2018, at a distance of 248,892,559\xa0km (1.664\xa0au) from the Sun.\n[\n4\n]\nThe maximum speed of the car relative to the Sun will be approximately 121,000\xa0km/h (75,000\xa0mph) at\nperihelion\n.\n[\n42\n]\nEven if the rocket had targeted an actual\nMars transfer orbit\n, the car could not have been placed into orbit around Mars, because the upper stage that carries it is not equipped with the necessary propellant, maneuvering, and communications capabilities. This flight simply demonstrated that Falcon Heavy is capable of launching significant payloads towards Mars in potential future missions.\n[\n40\n]\nCultural impact\n[\nedit\n]\nThe car in space quickly became a topic for\nInternet memes\n.\n[\n43\n]\n[\n44\n]\nWestern Australia Police\ndistributed a picture of a\nradar gun\naimed at the Roadster whilst above Australia.\n[\n45\n]\n[\n46\n]\nŠkoda\nproduced a\nparody\nvideo of a\nŠkoda Superb\nbeing driven to\nMars\n, a village in central France.\n[\n47\n]\n[\n48\n]\nAn attempt was made by\nDonut Media\nto launch a\nHot Wheels\nTesla Model X\nto the stratosphere using a\nweather balloon\n.\n[\n49\n]\n[\n50\n]\nToSky, a Russian start-up, sent a scale model of a Soviet-era\nLada\ncarrying a mannequin of Roscosmos head\nDmitry Rogozin\nto an altitude of 20\xa0km (12 miles) to gather test data for the design of\nstratostats\n.\n[\n51\n]\nSome news reports observed a similarity between the real pictures of a car orbiting the Earth and the title sequence of the animated\ncult classic\nfilm\nHeavy Metal\n(1981), where a space traveler lands on Earth in a 1950s two-seater\nChevrolet Corvette\nconvertible.\n[\n52\n]\n[\n53\n]\nThe SpaceX launch live stream reached over 2.3 million concurrent viewers on YouTube, which made it the second most watched live event on the platform, behind another space-related event:\nFelix Baumgartner\n\'s\njump from the stratosphere\nin 2012.\n[\n54\n]\nReactions\n[\nedit\n]\nThe choice of the Roadster as a dummy payload was variously interpreted as marketing for Tesla, or a work of art, with some worrying about the risk to contamination of otherwise sterile solar system bodies. Some also commented on how the Roadster was not a\nspace debris\nrisk.\nMarketing\n[\nedit\n]\nMusk was lauded as a savvy\nmarketer\nand\nbrand manager\nby controlling both the timing and the content of his corporate public relations.\n[\n55\n]\n[\n56\n]\n[\n57\n]\n[\n58\n]\nAfter the launch,\nScientific American\nsaid using a car was not entirely pointless, in the sense that something of that size and weight was necessary for a meaningful test.\n[\n55\n]\nAdvertising Age\nagreed with\nBusiness Insider\nthat the Roadster space launch was the "greatest ever car commercial without a dime spent on advertising", demonstrating that Musk is "miles ahead of the rest" in reaching young consumers, where "mere mortals scrabble about spending millions to fight each other over seconds of air time", Musk "just executes his vision."\n[\n56\n]\n[\n57\n]\nAlex Hern, technology reporter for\nThe Guardian\n, said the choice to launch a car was a "hybrid of genuine breakthrough and\nnerd\n-baiting publicity stunt" without "any real point beyond generating good press pics", which should not detract from the much more important technological milestone represented by the launch of the rocket itself.\n[\n59\n]\nLori Garver\n, a former NASA deputy director, initially said the choice of payload for the Falcon Heavy maiden flight is a\ngimmick\nand a loss of opportunity to further advance science—but later clarified that "I was told by a SpaceX VP (vice president) at the launch that they offered free launches to NASA, Air Force etc. but got no takers."\n[\n60\n]\nMusk responded to the critics by stating he wanted to inspire the public about the "possibility of something new happening in space," as part of his larger vision for\nspreading humanity to other planets\n.\n[\n8\n]\nWork of art\n[\nedit\n]\nMusk\'s Roadster mounted to a Falcon Heavy rocket\nThe Verge\nlikened the Roadster to a "\nready-made\n" work of art, such as\nMarcel Duchamp\n\'s 1917 piece\nFountain\n, created by placing an everyday object in an unusual position, context and orientation.\n[\n61\n]\nAlice Gorman\n, a lecturer in archaeology and space studies at\nFlinders University\nin Australia, said that the Roadster\'s primary purpose is symbolic communication, that "the red sports car symbolises\nmasculinity\n– power, wealth and speed\n[\n62\n]\n– but also how fragile masculinity is." Drawing on anthropological theories of symbols, she argues that "The car is also an armour against dying, a\ntalisman\nthat quells a profound fear of mortality."\n[\n63\n]\nGorman wrote that "the spacesuit is also about death. [...] The Starman was never alive, but now he\'s haunting space."\n[\n63\n]\nSpace debris non-risk\n[\nedit\n]\nOrbital debris expert Darren McKnight stated that the car poses no risk because it is far from Earth orbit. He added: "The enthusiasm and interest that [Musk] generates more than offsets the infinitesimally small \'littering\' of the cosmos."\n[\n64\n]\nTommy Sanford, director of the\nCommercial Spaceflight Federation\n, said that the car and its rocket stage are no more "space junk" than the mundane material usually launched on other test flights.\nMass simulators\nare often deliberately placed in a\ngraveyard orbit\nor sent on a\ndeep space\ntrajectory, where they are not a hazard.\n[\n65\n]\nBacteriological contamination\n[\nedit\n]\nThe Planetary Society\nwas concerned that launching a non-sterile object to interplanetary space may risk\nbiological contamination\nof a foreign world.\n[\n66\n]\nScientists at\nPurdue University\nnoted that the vehicle will be sterilized by solar radiation over time and the vehicle is most likely to hit the Earth in the future, though some bacteria might survive on some components of the vehicle which could contaminate Mars in the distant future if it were to hit Mars instead.\n[\n67\n]\nOrbit tracking\n[\nedit\n]\nThe car and the upper stage were\npassivated\nby intentionally removing remaining chemical and electrical energy, at which point they ceased transmitting\ntelemetry\n. Based on optical observations made using a robotic telescope at the Warrumbungle Observatory,\nDubbo\n, Australia and refinement of the orbit, a close re-encounter with Earth (originally predicted for 2073) is not possible.\n[\n68\n]\nIn October 2020 the car made a close approach to Mars, about 8\xa0million kilometres (5\xa0million miles) away, at which distance Mars\'s gravity had no significant effect on the Roadster\'s orbit.\n[\n69\n]\nThe\nVirtual Telescope Project\nobserved the Tesla two days after its launch, where it had an\napparent magnitude\nof 15.5,\n[\n70\n]\ncomparable to that of\nPluto\n\'s moon\nCharon\n. The Roadster was automatically spotted and logged by the\nAsteroid Terrestrial-impact Last Alert System\n(ATLAS) telescope operated by the\nUniversity of Hawaiʻi\n.\n[\n71\n]\nThe car was observed by the Deimos Sky Survey (DeSS) at a distance of 720,000\xa0km (450,000\xa0mi) with a flashing effect suggesting spinning.\n[\n72\n]\nRoadster photographed with a 0.43\xa0m telescope of Dubbo Observatory in Australia, on 8 February 2018, 16:29–16:50 UTC, at a distance of 550,000\xa0km (1.4 Lunar distances) from Earth. Varying brightness suggests spinning.\nThrough measuring changes in apparent brightness of the object, astronomers have determined that the Roadster is rotating with a period of 4.7589 ± 0.0060 minutes (i.e. 4 minutes, 46 seconds).\n[\n73\n]\nBy February 11, 2018,\nastrometry\nmeasurements from 241 independent observations had been collated, refining the positions to within one-tenth of an\narcsecond\nand published by the\nSeeSat-L\nmailing list, a group of amateur satellite spotters—more accurate than for most observations of objects in space.\n[\n74\n]\nIn 2025, the object was erroneously parsed as a new asteroid by a citizen astronomer going through archival\nCatalina Sky Survey\ndata and given the designation 2018 CN41 by the\nMinor Planet Center\n.\n[\n75\n]\n[\n76\n]\nThe object was correctly identified as the roadster eighteen hours later and deleted from the Minor Planet Center\'s archives.\n[\n77\n]\n[\n78\n]\nPredictions\n[\nedit\n]\nThe roadster made its first close approach to Mars on October 7, 2020. The next close approach to Earth will be in the year 2047 at a distance of 5 million kilometers, about 13 times the distance between Earth and the Moon.\n[\n69\n]\nSimulations over a 3-million-year timespan found a probability of the Roadster colliding with\nEarth\nat approximately 6%, or with\nVenus\nat approximately 2.5%. These probabilities of collision are similar to those of other\nnear-Earth objects\n. The\nhalf-life\nfor the tested orbits was calculated as approximately 20 million years, but with trajectories varying significantly following a close approach to the Earth–Moon system in 2091.\n[\n79\n]\nMusk had originally speculated that the car could drift in space for a billion years.\n[\n14\n]\nAccording to chemist William Carroll,\nsolar radiation\n,\ncosmic radiation\n, and\nmicrometeoroid\nimpacts will structurally degrade the car over time. Radiation will eventually break down any material with\ncarbon–carbon bonds\n, including\ncarbon fiber\nparts. Tires, paint, plastic and leather might have lasted only about a year, while carbon fiber parts will last considerably longer. Eventually, only the aluminum frame, inert metals, and glass not shattered by\nmeteoroids\nwill remain.\n[\n80\n]\nPotential follow up mission\n[\nedit\n]\nIn August 2019, as the Roadster completed its first orbit around the Sun,\n[\n81\n]\nMusk stated that SpaceX may one day launch a small spacecraft or\nStarship\nto catch up with the Roadster and take photographs or even return it to Earth for studying solar erosion on it just as\nApollo 12\ndid with\nSurveyor 3\nlander\'s components.\n[\n82\n]\nSee also\n[\nedit\n]\nList of artificial objects in heliocentric orbit\nList of passive satellites\nReferences\n[\nedit\n]\n^\na\nb\nc\nMiley, Jessica (February 9, 2018).\n"NASA Officially Lists Elon Musk\'s Floating Tesla Roadster As a Celestial Object"\n. She is the first ex-wife of businessman\nElon Musk\n.\nEarly life\n[\nedit\n]\nJustine Wilson was born in\nPeterborough, Ontario\n, and spent most of her early life there. She attended\nQueen\'s University\nin\nKingston, Ontario\n, and obtained a degree in English literature.\nCareer\n[\nedit\n]\nAfter college, Wilson moved to Japan, teaching\nEnglish as a second language\n(ESL). She subsequently settled in California.\n[\n1\n]\nWilson is the author of the\ncontemporary fantasy\nnovel\nBloodAngel\n,\n[\n5\n]\npublished in 2005 by the\nRoc Books\nimprint\nof\nPenguin Books\n. Her second book,\nUninvited\n, was released in 2007 and is an unrelated work intended for young-adult readers. A sequel to\nBloodAngel\n,\nLord of Bones\n, was released in 2008.\n[\n6\n]\nWilson was one of the first people to use a site like\nPinterest\nto plan out a novel.\n[\n7\n]\nIn a 2007 interview, she identified\nMargaret Atwood\n,\nJoyce Carol Oates\n,\nPaul Theroux\n,\nGeorge R.R. Martin\n,\nGuy Gavriel Kay\n, and\nNeil Gaiman\nas authors to whom she could relate her writings.\n[\n8\n]\nShe also described her books as cross-genre fiction.\nPersonal life\n[\nedit\n]\nIn January 2000, Wilson married\nElon Musk\n. Their first child was born in 2002 and died of\nsudden infant death syndrome\n(SIDS) at the age of 10 weeks.\n[\n1\n]\n[\n9\n]\nThrough\nin vitro fertilization\n, she gave birth to twins in 2004 and triplet boys in 2006.\n[\n10\n]\nOn September 13, 2008, she announced that she and Musk were getting a divorce.\n[\n11\n]\nShe and Musk shared custody of their children.\n[\n1\n]\nWilson later wrote an article for\nMarie Claire\ndetailing ways she thought the marriage was unhealthy, such as Musk\'s dismissal of her career ambitions, his description of himself as the "\nalpha\n" in the relationship, and his pressure for her to become a\ntrophy wife\n.\n[\n1\n]\n[\n12\n]\nIn 2010, she described herself as a "model former wife", and said she was on good terms with Musk\'s then-wife,\nTalulah Riley\n.\n[\n13\n]\n[\n14\n]\nShe has stated that she kept the last name Musk for the sake of their children.\n[\n15\n]\nIn 2022, one of their twins officially changed her name to\nVivian\nto reflect her\ngender identity\nand took Wilson as her surname because she no longer wished to be associated with her father.\n[\n16\n]\n[\n17\n]\nBibliography\n[\nedit\n]\nYear\nTitle\nPublisher\nISBN\nNotes\n2005\nBloodAngel\nRoc imprint, Penguin Books\nISBN\n9780451460523\n2007\nUninvited\nPaw
